From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  2 06:49:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 02 Jul 2001 00:49:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP and CGI error on Windows98 SE
In-Reply-To: <001001c10228$3c5a9000$5adefea9@sfingatron>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010702004921.007cd2e0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 02:20 PM 7/1/01 +0200, you wrote:
>   Hi,   I have a major problem. As I reinstalled my system  (windows 98
>SE), an error occures each time I try to start CGI or PHP script on  Xitami
>server. Before reinstalling Windows98 It worked oky, no problem reported. 
>But now I don't know what to do. As I start my page expl.:
>"http://localhost/test/test.php"  Windows just freeze and only hope to get
>back is CTRL+ALT+DEL and kill either  InternetExplorer or Winoldap (I think
>it is from windows to start old  applications). If I kill Winoldap then php
>executes script ok.   Where is the catch ? Does any one know, or is this 
>just another MS bug ?

Did you get all of the Windows updates for your system?  Usually installing
IE 5.5 fixes a majority of the bugs in Windows (IE actually has kernel
updates embedded as part of the package...some people don't really care
about IE, but the updates to the OS are worth having).  I recommend
installing all of the security updates, then updating IE to v5.5, then
running the remaining security updates.  (BTW, don't install Windows Media
Player 7.1...it doesn't do anything more than 6.4 does except consume 7MB
more RAM).

If that doesn't work, try re-installing Xitami using a more stable release.

I'm running Xitami v2.4d7 without any problems (yeah, I know about the DoS
bug that's fixed in the latest version...just haven't installed it yet).

Xitami tends crash on low-memory machines or machines that run out of
memory.  If you run Xitami regularly, then I suggest getting something like
RamIdle (RamIdle is freeware and I haven't had problems with it compared to
other packages) to keep enough memory free for Xitami under Windows.  I
haven't had problems with Xitami since I have 384MB RAM and usually have
around 150MB free.

Hope that helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  2 09:12:25 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (dimitri)
Date: Mon, 2 Jul 2001 09:12:25 +0100

>From earier thread and answer about SSi not working:

Folks,

There is another way, I think better. I have a site
http://www.altair7.com/index.html that uses a perl script for opening =
page,
see for your self.

I do not have the SSI_INSECURE set.  I do have MIME types defined as =
following
for the master config:

.pl =3D c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll
.cgi =3D c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll

This solved all my problems.

Steps:

1. http://127.0.0.1/admin
2. configuration -> mime
3. enter the above values
4. save
5. click on restart from the main page

Done.

With that done, then this works:

http://www.altair7.com/cgi-bin/od.pl

This works with xitami 2.4d1 through 7 and xitami pro versions.

Hope that helps, always make sure that you protect your perl scripts.

Cheers,
-Roberto

Patrick Olson wrote:
>=20
> This is how I got Perl running in Xitami
> it allows me to use,
>=20
> <!--#exec cgi=3D"/cgi-bin/test.pl" -->
>=20
> This SSI command
> which is a potential security risk for your system
> is only accepted if the environment variable
> SSI_INSECURE is set to 'yes'
> Under Windows NT
> in the System Control Panel
> under 'Environment
> =
-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=
=3D-
> Start->Settings->Control Panel
>=20
> Double click on System
>=20
> From the pop-up box select the Environment tab
>=20
>  In the Variable entry field type SSI_INSECURE
>  In the Value entry field type YES
>  (Make sure it goes where you want it,
>   System Variables probably.)
>=20
> Click OK
>=20
> Reboot?  (I don't know if this is required.)
> =
-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=3D-=
=3D-
>=20
> under Windows 95/98 by adding
> SET SSI_INSECURE=3Dyes to the autoexec.bat.
> to run SSI.
> If Perl is installed correctly?
> On a windows system,
> You then should be able to call
> Perl from anywhere in your system.
> This allows the shebang to be #! perl -w
> and does not need to be like this
> #! c:\perl\bin\perl.exe
> this also allows the use of
> #! /usr/bin/perl
> for the shebang. so as long
> as we don't use win32 specific modules
> or system calls we can keep our programs
> cross platform Compatible.
>=20
> Running Windows98
> Xitami v2.4d6
>=20
> in your
> autoexec.bat
>=20
> SET PATH=3DC:\PERL\BIN;%PATH%
> SET SSI_INSECURE=3DYES
>=20
> defaults.cfg
> [Filter]
>     .shtm=3Dperlssi
>     .shtml=3Dperlssi
>     .ssi=3Dperlssi
> [Ssi]
>     Enabled=3D1
>     Exec=3D1
>=20
> hope this helps
> http://www.isonline.com/xitami/2000/Jun/Msgs/l2w81135.html
> http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index5.htm
> http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index6.htm
>=20

  As I said before I´m having this kind of problems with xitami and perl cgi-
bin. I investigate a lot this kind of problem, and it happens not just with 
perl but also with php. The problem is not with xitami also. 
  The conclusion that I got is that the problem is with windows, more 
specifically in the user.exe program. There is a bug in this module related 
with dos prompt windows. They are not open during the execution of a cgi-bin, 
but in some way windows get lost with it. I don´t have a solution but a good 
point to start is searching about user.exe problems. By the way winoldap 
executes user.exe.
  I am afraid that there is no solution for this problem.

    Gustavo

> Did you get all of the Windows updates for your system?  Usually installing
> IE 5.5 fixes a majority of the bugs in Windows (IE actually has kernel
> updates embedded as part of the package...some people don't really care
> about IE, but the updates to the OS are worth having).  I recommend
> installing all of the security updates, then updating IE to v5.5, then
> running the remaining security updates.  (BTW, don't install Windows Media
> Player 7.1...it doesn't do anything more than 6.4 does except consume 7MB
> more RAM).
> 
> If that doesn't work, try re-installing Xitami using a more stable release.
> 
> I'm running Xitami v2.4d7 without any problems (yeah, I know about the DoS
> bug that's fixed in the latest version...just haven't installed it yet).
> 
> Xitami tends crash on low-memory machines or machines that run out of
> memory.  If you run Xitami regularly, then I suggest getting something like
> RamIdle (RamIdle is freeware and I haven't had problems with it compared to
> other packages) to keep enough memory free for Xitami under Windows.  I
> haven't had problems with Xitami since I have 384MB RAM and usually have
> around 150MB free.
> 
> Hope that helps!

Do you have these set in the
defaults.cfg file 

[Filter]
    .shtm=perlssi
    .shtml=perlssi 
    .ssi=perlssi   
[Ssi]
    Enabled=1
    Exec=1

however other than the Exec=1 the others are defult
and by defult testssi.ssi should work out of the box
make sure you have the path to perl set 

SET PATH=C:\PERL\BIN;%PATH%

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul  5 05:23:08 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Julian Rickards)
Date: Thu, 5 Jul 2001 00:23:08 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie can't setup virtual hosts
In-Reply-To: <000401c103aa$bff67bd0$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>
Message-ID: <200107050039672.SM00258@default>

Hi everyone:

If you have been following this thread, you will remember that I was 
able to get Xitami to deliver my local websites (ie on my hard drive) 
to my browser.  Because the current site I am developing cannot use 
SSI (their hosting package does not allow it and they don't want to 
pay for the upgrade), I have yet to test that feature.  However, 
absolute paths work perfectly.

The only drawback that I encounter is that everytime I want to 
browse a new page or refresh the current one, Win98SE wants me to 
connect to my ISP before it would show me the new page.  This was 
true with IE 5.5 and Opera 5.1 but when I tried Netscape 6.0, I found 
that I could cancel the dialup and it would show me the page I wanted 
to see.  Furthermore, because I cancelled the dialup, Netscape 6 did 
not ever ask for my ISP again which means that I can browse my 
"local" site as if I was not running Xitami.  It is slower than not using 
Xitami (I know that N6 is a bit of a pig too) but it is not 
unreasonable and the benefits of making my local site act like a 
"true" hosted site is tremendous.

Therefore, for anyone wanting to setup Xitami for the same 
purposes as myself would be recommended to use N6 as the test 
browser.

Jules

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 00:23:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (garry)
Date: Fri, 6 Jul 2001 11:23:33 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] problems with .pl .cgi and .exe
References: <200106221002.MAA27984@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <3B349500.825D0EC2@relativedata.com> <3B351BB1.885BE2C9@rci.rutgers.edu> <3B358861.85B29B74@qwest.net>
Message-ID: <000801c105a9$828ec0d0$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>

Hi people

i have had a very annoying problem that i finally figured out last week and
thought i might share with you all.

i found a neat php4 installer that included xitami in its list of servers
and having experienced the troubles that a lot of you mentioned here
installing php i decided to give it a shot.

when i chose xitami as the server it came back with a repy "sorry cant find
xitami".

i thought bugger .. and went off to get the lastest version assuming it was
installed into a different directory.

i was right and the installer worked fine, but after this i had problems
with some perl scripts that simply wouldnt work.

i chased the obvious paths etc and still nothing but noticed new scripts
added with the .pl extension worked fine.

last week i decided to sort it ..got the lastest version of xitami and perl
ran the installs and still a few scripts failed but as per before.
if i ran the old version of xitami i was using everything worked fine.

in the early days of hosting i had found that using no extension instead of
.pl or .cgi forced windows to rely on the #! perl line in the script so i
renamed realland.pl to realland , but also had a realland.exe in the cgi
bin.
now using /cgi-bin/realland my script worked but i didnt seem to be able to
change (edit)anything.

finally it hit me the realland script wasnt being accessed at all.
for some reason either xitami or win2k was giving  realland.exe the priority
and using that instead of realland and realland.pl gave a 500 error.

i renamed my realland.exe to reallandtest.exe and realland.pl started
working instantly as well as changes made in either realland or realland.pl
being visable.

my exe files are made with perl2xe if anyone wants to try and replicate this
problem

Garry Stanley

Cable.net.nz

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 16:24:02 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 06 Jul 2001 11:24:02 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] problems with .pl .cgi and .exe
References: <200106221002.MAA27984@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <3B349500.825D0EC2@relativedata.com> <3B351BB1.885BE2C9@rci.rutgers.edu> <3B358861.85B29B74@qwest.net> <000801c105a9$828ec0d0$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>
Message-ID: <3B45D812.C23AF9AA@rci.rutgers.edu>

> for some reason either xitami or win2k was giving  realland.exe the priority

Of course. Xitami looks for the exact name. If that fails, it tries the
name with EXE COM and BAT appended. If you ask for "foo", and there is
no "foo", it looks for "foo.exe", "foo.com", "foo.bat". 

So realland.exe will be found, and realland.pl won't be found unless you
give the full file name. 

> using no extension instead of .pl or .cgi forced windows to rely on the #! perl line in the script 

Actually, Windows does not know #! at all, Xitami is doing that. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 21:44:08 2001

Date: Fri, 6 Jul 2001 13:44:08 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Off Topic - IP Routing
In-Reply-To: "david" <webmaster@evernet.net>
 '[Xitami] Off Topic - IP Routing' (Jul  6, 11:28)
Message-ID: <200107061844.LAA16956@eskimo.com>

David,

You don't buy ip addresses. You purchase internet access from an ISP and they supply
your ip addresses. They buy big blocks and subdivide them. Sort of like a land
developer. You buy a domain name from one of the many places that are now selling them.
You can then have as many subdomains as you want, or that you can afford, depending on
your isp's requirements.

Good Luck!
Dennis

In message <5.1.0.14.2.20010706112008.021742e0@pop3.norton.antivirus>, Scott Ein
uis writes:
>Can Xitami be set to "wrap" the cgi so that ther server/script runs as a 
>certain "user" based on the folder ownership the script lies in?

At present, no.  Good idea though.  The closest thing is the setuid
features of Xitami (which currently work only under Unix; you can do
something similar with the service version for Windows NT); but the
setuid feature only lets you change which uid Xitami runs as once (and
all CGIs will also run as that uid).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 21:26:52 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 07 Jul 2001 08:26:52 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Screen Resolution...
In-Reply-To: Message from "Thomas J. Hruska" <shinelight@crosswinds.net>
 of "Thu, 28 Jun 2001 23:47:11 EST." <3.0.6.32.20010628234711.007a45c0@pop.crosswinds.net>
Message-ID: <200107062026.IAA22828@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20010628234711.007a45c0@pop.crosswinds.net>, "Thomas J. Hru
ska" writes:
>As I was playing around with IE, I noticed that the headers contain some
>extremely useful data that my CGI-based applications could use.  

As others have noted, these headers are non-standard, and basically only
an IE/IIS communication channel.

However that said, Xitami tries to make all the headers that it gets
available as HTTP_... headers to CGI/filter/LRWP programs if that
option is turned on (it is by default: [cgi] http-fields=1 and [cgi]
http-prefix=HTTP_).  So in theory I would expect the headers that you
mention to be available like that as well.

If this isn't happening for some reason we'd need to look at whether IE
is passing them as "real" headers, or as something else that is special.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 21:42:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 07 Jul 2001 08:42:33 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Refresh/Reload doesn't work
In-Reply-To: Message from "Dennis G. Wicks" <wix@eskimo.com>
 of "Fri, 29 Jun 2001 22:58:54 EST." <3B3D082E.30131.7D1FBF6@localhost>
Message-ID: <200107062042.IAA23245@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B3D082E.30131.7D1FBF6@localhost>, "Dennis G. Wicks" writes:
>Running V2.5b5 on NT 4.0 my browsers don't reload the page when 
>it has changed. I use IE 5.5 and Netscape 4.7. I have to force the 
>refresh or reload before I can see the changed page. (This is ctl-
>refresh in IE or shift-reload in Netscape.)

This is a browser feature: when browsers have something cached, they
send get-if-modified requests to see if they need a new copy of it,
which Xitami answers correctly.  However by default most browsers are
configured to check "once per session" -- which saves time and network
traffic, but can mean that you don't see the new page until you force a
reload if it changes during your session.

You can either change your browser setting, or force a reload -- or
force a particular page to not be cached (as others have described).

The only Xitami-related bit is that Xitami can be told to cache
index.html type defaults (to save opening/closing them all the time);
[server] cache-defaults=[0/1] controls this.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  6 22:14:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 07 Jul 2001 09:14:51 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Blocking
In-Reply-To: Message from russ@iron.dynip.com
 of "Wed, 04 Jul 2001 08:12:09 EST." <3B42CFD9.11867.2173B68@localhost>
Message-ID: <200107062114.JAA24683@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B42CFD9.11867.2173B68@localhost>, russ@iron.dynip.com writes:
>How does  one block a person from gettin on the web server?  is 
>there a way to  deny by ip in the defaults.aut?

You can set up a webmask list which denies that one address and allows
everything else _and_ allows access without a password.  But it may
block more than one person (eg, if they're using their ISPs proxy
cache), and may not block them completely (eg, if they have more than
one account).

If you need to explicitly block someone from a site that often means you
have to require everyone to log in, and then ban the person you don't
want.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul  7 22:05:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Sat, 7 Jul 2001 22:05:38 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Testing sites
References: <001b01c10722$e3464400$05811997@wes>
Message-ID: <008101c10728$94e35fe0$007968d5@rudge>

> it is done by default by Xitami, with the base address set at the pc name.
What I want to chenge is simply that base
> address. I hope I explained well my problem.

Do you mean that when you type http://www.geocities.com/ (for example), you
want to go to your local Xitami server? If so, then create a file named
"HOSTS" in the Windows directory (or edit it if it already exists), and add
the following line to it:

127.0.0.1    www.geocities.com

You don't need to set up any virtual hosts, etc, in Xitami.

Owen Rudge
http://www.owenrudge.co.uk/
http://www.gamearchive.uk.tt/


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul  7 22:19:03 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sat, 07 Jul 2001 16:19:03 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Testing sites
In-Reply-To: <001b01c10722$e3464400$05811997@wes>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010707161903.007c4b70@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 10:14 PM 7/7/01 +0200, you wrote:
>   Hi, I'm a new Xitami user. I want to use it just to  test the websites I
>create, including server-side scripts, etc. What I want to  do is to have
>the possibility to browse a site with the browser in "online" mode  and
>using full addresses. For example suppose I create a site at the address
>www.geocities.com/my site; I create  my pages including full addresses in
>links, images etc., identical to the pages  that will be published on the
>geocities server. What I want to do is testing the  site when it's on my
>local hard disk but typing the correct full address on the  browser which
>is set in "online" mode. Is it possible? I think yes, because it  is done
>by default by Xitami, with the base address set at the pc name. What I 
>want to chenge is simply that base address. I hope I explained well my 
>problem. Thanks in advance, Franco 

Actually you can't do that unless you host your own DNS server as well...of
course you would then not be able to upload anything to geocities.com until
you disabled the DNS server, uploaded, then re-enabled the DNS server.
That's too much of a pain in the neck if you ask me.

My question is, if you are using a static host for your site, why bother
with a web server?  You can write static-HTML on your computer and it will
look the same both locally and remotely (providing the remote host doesn't
use case-sensitive filenames...but that just requires a bit of fore-thought
- and Xitami is _NOT_ a case-sensitive server under Windows).

All the "online" and "offline" browsing modes do is determine whether to
use already cached pages or to get them from the remote server.  It really
has little relation to web page development since you want to be in
"online" mode anyway or nothing will change when you reload the page.

If you want to have more power, you can host your own web page with
Xitami...which is what its true purpose is.  If all you are going to do is
create static webpages for some other host, you are probably missing the
point of a web server (the point is to serve web pages from your computer
to other people...not to test static pages to upload to geocities).  I
suggest checking out <http://www.dhs.org/>.  It may be a bit confusing for
you, but I highly recommend their dynamic DNS service if you want to host
your own website (and don't have a static IP address).

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

The FTP Server is shut off on both, and on the standard, HTTP runs on

On Sun, 10 Sep 2000 17:01:16 -0500, you wrote:


-------
In message <3412787957.20000702175610@yahoo.co.uk>, Peter Adams
writes:
>Xitami is suspended on my system. Why is this? I don't want it
>suspended but this past two days it's been suspended. It starts as
>normal then suspends itself with a little window coming up saying
>"HTTP service started at 02/Jul/2000; 17:54:48 +0000"

Xitami normally only suspends itself (automatically) when it cannot
talk
to the network for some reason.  Looking in the log might give you
some
idea what it is having problems with (eg, the console.log) in
situations
like this.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  8 04:57:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sat, 07 Jul 2001 22:57:23 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Suspended
In-Reply-To: <uhlfktk9msj2382avfcphv08k4odmhe8nh@4ax.com>
References: <200009102057.IAA05752@pagoda.wgtn.naos.co.nz>
 <200009102057.IAA05752@pagoda.wgtn.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010707225723.007b6a60@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 10:40 PM 7/7/01 -0500, you wrote:
>I am running two versions of Xitami, the standard, and the Pro.
>
>I've been running the standard for several months with no problems,
>but now I go to run the Pro alongside it, and everytime it starts, it
>suspends itself. Is there any way around this? I checked the logs, and
>it's not showing any errors at all. 
>
>The FTP Server is shut off on both, and on the standard, HTTP runs on
>port 80. On the Pro, I set a port base of 10, so HTTP runs at 90, but
>HTTPS still runs at 443, it seems to be working fine, but just
>suspends itself on start up.
>
>Thank you for any ideas with this.
>Jeff

Pro runs in console mode if you are running v2.4c1.  Just press Ctrl-C to
stop it and it should shut down cleanly.  Not sure about more recent
versions of Pro.

If you put the standard version in the same directory as the Pro version,
then there will be conflicts with the configurations (Xitami standard might
be detecting changes to log files and thus suspends itself).  You should
re-install both and put them in separate directories.  To make both
versions work well together in separate directories, point Pro's Xitami.cfg
[Server]->webpages variable to the standard's webpages directory...be sure
to spell out the directory path letter for letter (e.g. Program Files, not
Progra~1) or you will get strange errors.  You can point Standard to Pro,
they should just point to the same place.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  8 08:18:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 08 Jul 2001 19:18:14 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Running 2 Servers on 1 Computer
In-Reply-To: Message from jeff <jeff@jcswebhosting.com>
 of "Sun, 08 Jul 2001 01:51:41 EST." <te0gktohtegce6a66ntulpjlt3nsbmha34@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <200107080718.TAA19221@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <te0gktohtegce6a66ntulpjlt3nsbmha34@4ax.com>, jeff writes:
>Do I just run the Pro version, and have it handle everything,
>including Virtual Hosting? 

Sure.  Unless you've got a specific reason for having both Xitami/Pro
and Xitami running (some dramatically different configuration that
cannot be merged together), then Xitami/Pro can do everything that
Xitami will do "and more".  So you need only run Xitami/Pro: it'll
handle virtual hosting, HTTP/HTTPS/FTP, etc.  HTTPS virtual hosting is
tricky (needs to be IP address based) but if you're using HTTPS only for
a single secure order site that shouldn't be an issue.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

until
> you disabled the DNS server, uploaded, then re-enabled the DNS server.
> That's too much of a pain in the neck if you ask me.
>
> My question is, if you are using a static host for your site, why bother
> with a web server?  You can write static-HTML on your computer and it will
> look the same both locally and remotely (providing the remote host doesn't
> use case-sensitive filenames...but that just requires a bit of
fore-thought
> - and Xitami is _NOT_ a case-sensitive server under Windows).
>
> All the "online" and "offline" browsing modes do is determine whether to
> use already cached pages or to get them from the remote server.  It really
> has little relation to web page development since you want to be in
> "online" mode anyway or nothing will change when you reload the page.
>
> If you want to have more power, you can host your own web page with
> Xitami...which is what its true purpose is.  If all you are going to do is
> create static webpages for some other host, you are probably missing the
> point of a web server (the point is to serve web pages from your computer
> to other people...not to test static pages to upload to geocities).  I
> suggest checking out <http://www.dhs.org/>.  It may be a bit confusing for
> you, but I highly recommend their dynamic DNS service if you want to host
> your own website (and don't have a static IP address).
>
> Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  8 13:49:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Sun, 08 Jul 2001 12:49:44 GMT
Subject: [Xitami] asp question
Message-ID: <43107@dsl.co.uk>

In message <20010708040353.51272.qmail@web9505.mail.yahoo.com>
   Dragonballz Insane writes:
> I'm running Xitami on Windows ME and had a question.
> Does Xitami support ASP Active Server Documents and if
> so do I need a interperter like Active Perl for perl
> and cgi scripts

As Ewan has said, there are third-party add-ons which will work with
Xitami (amongst other http daemons) to provide ASP.

One that I have tried is iASP == instant ASP from HalcyonSoft.  If you go
to http://www.halcyonsoft.com/ and navigate your way around the menus,
you will find that there is a "developer's edition" which is a free
download (after answering some questions).  This is a slightly limited
version of the full commercial product, in that one is limited to only
ten sessions (the web site says two, but Halcyon have assured me that
it's ten).

I had been intending to use this, along with Xitami, to provide a
platform for an annual "DIY e-Commerce" course that we run at the end of
our undergraduates' first year.  Unfortunately, I discovered a gaping
hole in Halcyon's implementation of VBScript; one cannot instantiate the
RegExp class.  Since some of the lecturer's code depends upon using this
(and other classes), iASP was not "fit for purpose", so sadly this year
we did as in previous years and used M$'s IIS 4.0 --- a shame, because we
wanted to encourage the thought-process that Microsoft is not the only
way of doing things.

Halcyon assured me that this "bug" would be fixed in v2.0 of iASP, but
with a fixed timescale we did not have the luxury of waiting for this to
be released.

Incidentally, iASP works on other platforms apart from Windoze, so with
Xitami provides an ASP capability of Linux, for example.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk

    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  8 20:32:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 09 Jul 2001 07:32:49 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] How-to? Set up multiple web sites using a single static IP address
In-Reply-To: Message from Andrew Tate <a.tate@surrey.ac.uk>
 of "Tue, 26 Jun 2001 17:51:04 +0100." <3.0.6.32.20010626175104.00ad0c80@pop.surrey.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <200107081932.HAA24071@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20010626175104.00ad0c80@pop.surrey.ac.uk>, Andrew Tate writes:
>Others have already replied and given some information.  The way the server 
>decides on which site to serve up is the name given in the http request.  [...]
>However, this only works in recent browsers and may not be supported with 
>light wap phones etc - I don't know.  

The Host: header is compulsory in HTTP/1.1, which has been out for about
2 years IIRC.  It was widely supported before that, and pretty much
everything that has been produced in the last 5-6 years has used the
Host: header.  Basically I don't see any problem using Host:-based
virtual hosting any longer; there are very very few people using the
older HTTP/0.9 and HTTP/1.0-without-Host: browsers now, and a lot of
sites that won't work for them if they continue to do so.

If you're really bothered, put all the virtual hosts in subdirectories
and make the base configuration point at each subdirectory so that users
can choose which one that they want.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>still http://mycomputername. What can I do?

The default hostname _will_ be the name of your computer.  Providing you
use HTTP/1.1-style Host: headers everything should work fine anyway; but
if you really can't do that, you can override [Server] hostname.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  9 13:31:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Mon, 09 Jul 2001 07:31:54 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Testing sites
References: <200107081957.HAA24704@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz> <3B4917F6.99D1632A@home.com> <3B491E04.911D1C72@home.com>

I dug this out of the archives for you:

---------------------------------------------------

Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question - mult. domains
Date: Mon, 12 Jun 2000 16:03:53 -0500
From: "Kartic Krishnamurthy" <kaygee@netset.com>
Reply-To: Xitami@isonline.com
To: <Xitami@isonline.com>

Ron,

This is just an example...
1) defaults.cfg
[Virtual-Hosts]
www.douglasdemocrat.com=dd.cfg # site www.douglasdemocrats.com
www.orangekitty.com=ok.cfg     # site www.orangekitty.com
douglasdemocrat.com=dd.cfg # what if someone just types in
                           # douglasdemocrats or organgekitty.com?!
orangekitty.com=ok.cfg     # ....this handles that!

[Server]
Webpages=webpages

Now, do not put anything under webpages or the default pages you would like
served, say for my_business_domain.com (your
business!?).

2) dd.cfg
[Server]
Webpages=c:\douglasdemocrats (or /var/douglasdemocrats or whatever)

c:\douglasdemocrats -> all your files related to the democratic party of
douglas county
3) ok.cfg
[Server]
Webpages=c:\orangekitty

c:\orangekitty -> all files related to orang kitty web site

Now, remember if you IP address is 111.222.333.444, you _must_ have DNS
records setup (or request your ISP to do) such that both
these domains point to your server's IP address (111.222.333.444).  This is
the key for the whole setup to work!

Hope this helps.

---------------------------------------------------

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  9 20:01:45 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 10 Jul 2001 07:01:45 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Forcing https.
In-Reply-To: Message from Zdenko =?iso-8859-1?Q?Roh=E1=E8?= <Zdenko.Rohac@tuke.sk>
 of "Tue, 26 Jun 2001 14:18:16 +0200." <5.0.2.1.0.20010626140940.0235b080@ccsun.tuke.sk>
Message-ID: <200107091901.HAA03689@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <5.0.2.1.0.20010626140940.0235b080@ccsun.tuke.sk>, Zdenko =?iso-8859-1?Q?Roh=E1=E8?= writes:
>My website is composed from some static pages and web applications.
>I would like to use http protocol for static pages and secure https for
>applications. But I was not able to figure out how to force using https
>for defined directory.

There isn't a way to do this at present (although it's a good idea,
which has been suggested before).  Generally for most sites forcing
HTTPS doesn't gain you very much other than avoiding the possibility of
users accidentally sending things in plain text they might not want to
do so.  However that's usually balanced against allowing users to do so
if they're really not able to use HTTPS.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

changes under BeOS now, so if someone is interested in recompiling it,
please feel free.

For example the images located in ./webpages/images do not load
>if I type http://localhost/images/image_1.gif, but they do if I type
>http://localhost//images/image_1.gif. On the other hand
>./webpages/xitami/images works fine and
>http://localhost/xitami/images/image_1.gif displays as desired. 

This is rather puzzling.  It's almost as if the path definitions are
wrong.  You might want to turn on server debugging mode ([Server] debug=1)
and see what path locations it is trying with each request.  And you
might also want to compare the configuration file in the Windows version
(or source package) with the ones in the BeOS one, just in case they are
wrong for some reason.

>Another serious issue for me is that when Xitami is started, cpu load for my
>amd duron 750 goes up to 100% and stays there until I stop the server. I
>have no idea what's going wrong. 

It sounds like it's getting stuck in a loop for some reason.  Normally
Xitami should "go to sleep" waiting for the OS to tell it that someone
has sent it a request to deal with.  For some reason this doesn't seem
to be happening for you.

Has anyone else found this with the BeOS version?  (I don't have access
to a BeOS version to test.)

If there's anyone who's built Xitami from source under BeOS, they could
perhaps turn on the tracing functions and try to figure out where it is
looping.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

our bug list.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  9 20:13:35 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 10 Jul 2001 07:13:35 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] What's different about the XITAMI FTP server that makes it work with the Windows 98 FTP client?
In-Reply-To: Message from Andrew Tate <a.tate@surrey.ac.uk>
 of "Thu, 28 Jun 2001 11:24:20 +0100." <3.0.6.32.20010628112420.008be100@pop.surrey.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <200107091913.HAA03980@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20010628112420.008be100@pop.surrey.ac.uk>, Andrew Tate writes:
>Sometimes ftp servers can 'restrict to home directory' and stop browsing
>outside of the home directory tree defined for the user.  Other times
>you may not see the other disks (as ftp has roots in unix) so is not used 
>to the disk drive letter idea but if you put 'cd d:/' it may take it and 
>act correctly.

Xitami doesn't handle drive letters like that (as you say, some Windows
based FTP servers do).  Instead Xitam insists that you define an alias
that points at the other drive, and that people use that alias instead.

As you've found there are some issues with the Xitami FTP support, and
it doesn't always seem to play nicely with others.  A number of these
issues are on our bug list, but meanwhile if you need some of the
features in other FTP servers you are probably better disabling the
internal FTP server in Xitami, and using another one alongside it.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  9 20:16:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 10 Jul 2001 07:16:56 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] PHP and CGI error on Windows98 SE
In-Reply-To: Message from "Vladimir Domjan jr." <vladimir.domjan@tutokameni.com>
 of "Sun, 01 Jul 2001 14:20:35 +0200." <001001c10228$3c5a9000$5adefea9@sfingatron>
Message-ID: <200107091916.HAA04029@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001001c10228$3c5a9000$5adefea9@sfingatron>, "Vladimir Domjan jr." writes:
>I have a major problem. As I reinstalled my system (windows 98 SE), an 
>error occures each time I try to start CGI or PHP script on Xitami 
>server. Before reinstalling Windows98 It worked oky, no problem 
>reported. But now I don't know what to do.
>As I start my page expl.: "http://localhost/test/test.php" Windows just 
>freeze and only hope to get back is CTRL+ALT+DEL and kill either 
>InternetExplorer or Winoldap (I think it is from windows to start old 
>applications). If I kill Winoldap then php executes script ok.

This sounds very strange.  It sounds like Windows is causing problems
with Xitami trying to run programs.  We've seen this occassionally if
you have a virus scanner running, or some other security product that
tries to restrict what programs can do (Xitami needs to be able to run
other programs, to do CGI/filters).  

If you do have a virus scanner running or some other security product,
try disabling it briefly and see if the problem with Xitami and
CGI/filters goes away.  If it does, it's a conflict between the two
things.

If you don't have either a virus scanner or security product running, it
sounds a bit like something has got messed up with your Windows install
-- although that's a little suspicious given that it sounds like a
relatively recent install.  But sometimes Windows is just like that :-(

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 10 04:27:30 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 09 Jul 2001 22:27:30 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Refreshing the Xitami IP address
In-Reply-To: <LPBBKCGLHJHGFKBNPPHMAEIOCGAA.gerry6362@startrekmail.com>
References: <200107081001.MAA14906@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010709222730.007e17e0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 03:48 PM 7/8/01 -0500, you wrote:
>I've been a lurker for some time now, I'm using Xitami on a win98 machine
>with all the current updates and a dynamic dial up IP (hoping someone will
>offer cable or DSL where we live soon). What I'm looking for is a piece of
>software that will detect when my machine goes on and off line and close and
>start Xitami at the appropriate times so that the IP address is correct.
>I've tried using ICQ and Net cruiser, both will run Xitami but it closes 2
>seconds later and unfortunately if either of these managed to start the
>server they don't offer the facility to close it when the computer gets
>disconnected.
>
>I hope this explains my dilemma, anybody got any ideas?

To start Xitami from another program is fairly simple to do (e.g. the
system() command in C).

To shut down Xitami from another program is a bit more difficult:
First, enumerate all the Windows and loop through them until you run into
the window name "xiwin32" or "xitami" or something like that.
Then, send a WM_QUIT message to it (or you could try sending the
appropriate message to suspend Xitami instead - WM_QUIT is easier, though).
 Xitami should shut down.

Look under the RAS Services section of MSDN for details on connection
information.

So, here is how your program would work:

1)  Wait for RAS to connect successfully to the Internet.
2)  Start Xiami.
3)  Wait for RAS to disconnect.
4)  Shut down Xitami.
5)  Repeat until you cause your program to quit.

I don't think there is any other way to accomplish what you want to do.
So, now might be a good time to learn how to write Windows programs.
Otherwise, keep searching - there is probably a utility, I just don't need
to use it (cable modems are very nice - 100-200K/sec transfers on avg.).


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

>>applications. But I was not able to figure out how to force using https
>>for defined directory.
>
>There isn't a way to do this at present (although it's a good idea,

Apache uses HTTPS="on" as well as setting SSL environment information to
let CGI applications know that they are being run on a secure protocol.  I
think setting HTTPS="on" is enough for 99% of the CGIs being run out there.

>windows 98 especially, but also win95, goes in search of any existing
>version of windows on your hard drive ..in my experience it then cheats and

>
>assuming you reinstalled cause you had a problem the odds are this problem

I keep trying to tell people to re-install IE 5.5 and the security updates
first before re-installing Windows...and if they haven't, then do so.  IE
has _kernel updates_ embedded in it that will repair ailing OSes.  I've
literally brought PCs back from the dead (one had 4 different viruses on it
and they had trashed a lot of the data) just by (re)installing IE (which
restored the OS data - F-PROT took care of the remaining mess).

I don't use a real-time virus scanner either.  I just use a good ol' DOS
program called F-PROT and maintain my knowledge of how viruses *REALLY*
work (many people think they are magical and McAfee is magical too...or
something like that - guess what...neither are magical).  F-PROT is
freeware, scans more viruses than McAfee's bloated piece of junk, and is
the tool of choice for removing viruses from virtually-dead machines (even
viruses designed for Windows).

Finally, Xitami and CGIs will crash if there is not enough memory
available.  Suggestion:  Install RamIdle.  It is an excellent freeware
product.

Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 12 08:33:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 12 Jul 2001 19:33:50 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] ftp problem
In-Reply-To: Message from Deepak Adlakha <deepakad_2000@yahoo.com>
 of "Thu, 12 Jul 2001 00:25:32 MST." <20010712072532.23084.qmail@web5501.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200107120733.TAA27447@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <20010712072532.23084.qmail@web5501.mail.yahoo.com>, Deepak Adlakha w
rites:
>By default xitami is running on Http -80 and ftp -21.
>Now if i change Http to any other port like 1080 and
>ftp will become-1021.Now when i say ftp from dos
>prompt.Then it say connection refused.

Currently the only way to change the HTTP port is to change the port
base, which shifts _everything_ up by that base amount, including FTP.

Some FTP clients let you specify which port number to connect to, in
this case 1021, eg:

ftp HOSTNAME PORT

which may let you work around that.

Alternatively as a work around you can set the FTP port in the
configuration file to a sufficient negative number to offset the amount
it is shifted, and get you back to the standard port 21, eg, (21-1000) =
-979.

This is on our bug list, and eventually there'll be a way to change just
the HTTP port number.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 13 21:44:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 13 Jul 2001 16:44:49 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Off Topic Perl Programmer
References: <3B4F4AB4.D7FCB6CF@evernet.net>
Message-ID: <3B4F5DC1.40065460@rci.rutgers.edu>

> take a perl script I have and make it so that I can pass form values to it. I know just about nothing when it comes to perl 

Xitami parses form values into the Environment with the prefix "POST_"
(this can be configured). 

Perl lets you read the Environment in an array called $ENV{}. Note the
curly-braces... in some fonts they look like parenthesis, but aren't!

If the form has fields named "name" and "gender", use this to print the
values: 

 print "Name            $ENV{FORM_name}\n";
 print "Gender          $ENV{FORM_gender}\n";

Instead of "print", you can assign to variables and do something else.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 13 22:22:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 13 Jul 2001 17:22:34 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Off Topic Perl Programmer
References: <3B4F4AB4.D7FCB6CF@evernet.net>
Message-ID: <3B4F669A.F4520B8F@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  <Input type="Text" name="Name" value="David">

> print "$ENV{FORM_name}\n"

Perl variable names are case sensitive. name is not the same as Name. 

> it doesn't show me anything on the page.

Always have some simple literal text that "must" display, without any
tricky variables or calculations: 

 print "Hello there! You typed: \n";

Then you know if the script is sick, or you just printed an invalid
variable. 

> The script doesn't return any errors....

The script you cited will never barf-back errors (they may go out into a
log file, but in this case probably not). 

Start all your CGI Perl scripts with this: 

 use strict;
 use CGI qw(:standard);
 use CGI::Carp qw(fatalsToBrowser);

"strict" will catch many "easy" errors. 

The "fatalsToBrowser" option of CGI Carp will send error messages to you
(in the browser) rather than in some obscure log file. You "may" want to
disable this when your script runs perfectly; but in debugging it is a
real time saver.

There is an even better version of this error catching code but I don't
have it handy. It catches compile-time errors and lets you set a custom
message. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 13 22:46:45 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 14 Jul 2001 09:46:45 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Hosts
In-Reply-To: Message from "Brian Leiter" <info@pcgamblinggames.com>
 of "Fri, 13 Jul 2001 16:32:34 -0400." <001401c10bda$f34117b0$0100a8c0@leiter1>
Message-ID: <200107132146.JAA11289@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001401c10bda$f34117b0$0100a8c0@leiter1>, "Brian Leiter" writes:
>Help me please... I am running Xitami 2.5b5 on Windows 2000.  When I 
>FIRST setup the virtual hosts everything was fine... Then Xitami started 
>crashing in the admin config section and now they don't work?  I even 
>uninstalled Xitami and reinstalled it with NO LUCK on getting the 
>virtual hosts to work again.

Did you start with a new set of configuration files?  If not it sounds
like it might be in your configuration file.  Xitami tries to recognise
the host name passed in and use that to figure out which directory to
use: for some reason it sounds like in your case the names aren't
matching.  You'd probably be best checking spelling, etc, carefully.  Or
turning on the server debugging ([Server] debug=1), and checking the
debug log carefully for what Xitami is doing internally.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 14 00:19:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Fri, 13 Jul 2001 18:19:36 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Off Topic Perl Programmer
In-Reply-To: <3B4F4AB4.D7FCB6CF@evernet.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010713181936.007b3cb0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 12:23 PM 7/13/01 -0700, you wrote:
>Hi All,
>
>I need someone to take a perl script I have and make it so that
>I can pass form values to it. I know just about nothing when it
>comes to perl thats why I was looking for someone to help.
>
>Anyone able to offer a hand? It's very very simple. I can do it
>in cold fusion but not in Perl. Thanks,
>
>david

The following two functions will extract each value from STDIN (where form
values are placed) and put them into a hash.  Just use '&ParseForm();'
(without the quotes) to parse the data into the 'values' hash, then you
access your form variables using '$values{FormName}' to access each
individual element of the form data.

sub ParseForm
{
  local ($fields, $name, $value, $data);

  read(STDIN, $data, $ENV{"CONTENT_LENGTH"});
  @fields = split(/&/, $data);

  foreach $item (@fields)
  {
    ($name, $value) = split(/=/, $item);
    $name = &UnescapeString($name);
    $value = &UnescapeString($value);
    $values{$name} = $value;
  }
}

sub UnescapeString
{
  local ($s) = $_[0];
  local ($pos, $ascii);

  $s =~ s/\+/ /g;       # Replace the + sign with spaces

  $pos = 0;             # Replace %xx with hexadecimal
  while (($pos = index($s, "%", $pos)) != -1)
  {
    $ascii = hex(substr($s, $pos + 1, 2));
    substr($s, $pos, 3) = pack("c", $ascii);
  }
  $s;
}


Hope that helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 14 02:24:08 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 14 Jul 2001 13:24:08 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Custom Errors
In-Reply-To: Message from "Brian Leiter" <info@pcgamblinggames.com>
 of "Fri, 13 Jul 2001 20:32:41 -0400." <001801c10bfc$7e707d50$0100a8c0@leiter1>
Message-ID: <200107140124.NAA12753@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001801c10bfc$7e707d50$0100a8c0@leiter1>, "Brian Leiter" writes:
>I know about @error/text-404.htm, the header and footer but for some 
>reason all I get is the STANDARD IE 404 error from internet explorer.

The @error/text-404.htm is how you get a custom error message.  But only
if the browser is willing to display it.  IE has its own ideas, and by
default displays a "simplified" (read: useless (IMHO)) error message
instead.  Any IE user that wants to see your customised 404 errors will
have to display this feature (called something like "simplified error
messages") in their IE configuration.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Ah ha.  If you've got two things writing to the same temporary directory
using similar file names that could be bad.

We've always said that if you are going to run two instances of Xitami,
you should run them in different directories.  Obviously if you are
using dynamic content this should include different temp directories as
well.

I'm curious about the "bazillion" pipe files though -- which version of
Xitami are you using?  Do you have any debugging options turned on?
(We've had this issue reported before but I thought it had been resolved
providing the debug options were all off -- if the debug options are on,
Xitami keeps them around to assist with debugging.)

of the TEMP environment variable (if present) or the temp directory.
Just override one of them with some other setting.

for production use.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul 15 10:08:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 15 Jul 2001 21:08:57 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] POST troubles (longish)
In-Reply-To: Message from Boyan Brezinsky <boyan@sanbolic.com>
 of "Fri, 13 Jul 2001 14:05:04 +0300." <01C10BA4.D1051D80.boyan@sanbolic.com>
Message-ID: <200107150908.VAA06049@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <01C10BA4.D1051D80.boyan@sanbolic.com>, Boyan Brezinsky writes:
>Here is the story. Yesterday downloaded dcl - a project tracking system 
>written in PHP. At startup you have to login, supplying username and 
>password.  [Get 404 error when use Login]

There's two things that could be generating the 404: Xitami and PHP.
I can't remember off hand if Xitami logs a 404 only when it generates
it, or when that's the code it's going to return (which a CGI/filter can
supply).

Since the request/debug log entries you supply don't match up with the
times in the other snippets you supply, it's hard to know exactly what
is going on.

However I'd definitely suggest (a) looking for messages in cgierr.log,
and (b) adding something to the PHP so you can tell if it is being run.
The fact that Xitami seems to be trying to transfer .flt files (filter
files), suggests that something must have generated those files to
transfer.

You might also want to enable [cgi] debug=1 (which controls filtering
too) and let it preserve the filter files (normally they are removed
after being sent).  Then you can check the contents of those to see if
it is PHP that is writing the 404 error (or indeed if it is writing
anything).

Given that you seem to have a working PHP setup in general (since some
of your other PHP works) I suspect that looking closely at what the
problem PHP script is doing/trying to do has to be your next step.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul 15 10:12:01 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 15 Jul 2001 21:12:01 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] errors.gsl
In-Reply-To: Message from "Ben Wheare" <maples@x-stream.co.uk>
 of "Tue, 03 Jul 2001 16:50:25 +0100." <006d01c103d7$eb837f00$617969d5@ben>
Message-ID: <200107150912.VAA06170@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <006d01c103d7$eb837f00$617969d5@ben>, "Ben Wheare" writes:
>Any1 know how to use the errors. gsl file to produce a replia of the apache
>type. I.e. display a customized message, title e.t.c???

errors.gsl is basically a template file for what to output, with the
bits in $(....) being values that Xitami has set which you can
substitute into the HTML.  There's a list of which values are available
at the top of the file (in comments).

So essentially you need to edit the HTML in there to match what you
want, using $(...) to put in values that Xitami has from the request
where you want them.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In message <27.17ff19be.287a7650@cs.com>, Cwmoreland@cs.com writes:
>I'm currently on my Win2000 machine. Only console.log has a line that is 
>questionable: 
>2001/07/08 22:28:19: smtpipe: 'pipedef.xml' not found

This is just a warning; if you're not using the pipe control feature you
don't have to have this file.

>Debug.log does not have anything. When I load default.htm and click on the 
>SSI link (for testssi.ssi) the page loads EXCEPT for the stuff in 
>testssi.inc. When I view the page source in Explorer the SSI line has been 
>passed through unparsed:
>
><P>If SSI is working and enabled, you will see the various SSI tags
>correctly translated below.
><!--#include file="testssi.inc"-->
>.....
>
>I also notice that the GIF images in the test webpages don't show up. 

Are you _sure_ you're loading your pages through Xitami?  Both those
problems sound a whole lot like you're just getting IE to load the files
form disk -- in which case it's no surprise that Xitami isn't doing any
SSI translation: no one is asking Xitami to do so.

You should be using a URL like:

http://localhost/

when you are testing.  Not one file file:///.....

The file:///.... one would have problems with image urls like "/image/...";
but Xitami would definitely find them in the default configuration with
a url like that.  This would also explain your empty access.log, and
empty debug.log.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 16 15:45:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Boyan Brezinsky)
Date: Mon, 16 Jul 2001 17:45:09 +0300
Subject: [Xitami] RE: POST troubles (longish)
Message-ID: <01C10E1F.0F9877F0.boyan@sanbolic.com>

Thanks for the tips. I've found and worked around the problem, now the 
question is if it is a bug in Xitami or some misunderstanding by the 
developer of dcl.
On login, dcl sends user name, password and so on to login.php3.
login.php3 in turn calls its own function Refresh(). This function is used 
to redirect the server to a new file - main.php3 or listFrame.php3, 
depending on your choice of frames or not.
The Refresh() function can use two types of redirect - through the php 
Header() function or through html meta tags.
The relevant part is:
		if ($GLOBALS['cookieMethod'] == 'header')
		{
			$hdr = '';
			if ($GLOBALS['redirMethod'] == 'php')
				$hdr = "Location: $toHere\n";

			$hdr .= "Set-Cookie: DCLINFO=$theCookie\n";
			$hdr .= "Set-Cookie: DCLTYPEMENU=$DCLUI\n";
			$hdr .= "\r\n";

			Header($hdr);
			if (substr($toHere, 0, 10) == 'index.php3')
				exit;
		}
<snip some code>
		print('<html><head>');
<snip a little more>	
		print("<meta http-equiv=\"refresh\" content=\"00;URL=$toHere\">");
		print('</head>');
<and snip till end of function>

In the non-working configuration I have $redirMethod=="php" and 
$cookieMethod=="header"
In the working configuration the $redirMethod is set to "meta".
In both cases the $toHere variable gets the value 
"main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show" (actually, the php3 filename depends on 
the type of the interface, but this is not important here). Unfortunately, 
it is hard-coded: Refresh('main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show', $id, 
$thispwd, $GLOBALS['DCLUI'], $GLOBALS['LANG'], $GLOBALS['DOMAIN']);

In the non-working case the generated output is (from *.flt):
X-Powered-By: PHP/4.0.4
Location: main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show
Set-Cookie: DCLINFO=1/0/dfe2c07de313f0d7ca27146e068767f1/en/default
Set-Cookie: DCLTYPEMENU=0
Content-type: text/html

<html><head><meta http-equiv="refresh" 
content="00;URL=main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show"></head>



In the working case ($redirMethod=="meta") the generated output is:
X-Powered-By: PHP/4.0.4
Set-Cookie: DCLINFO=1/0/dfe2c07de313f0d7ca27146e068767f1/en/default
Set-Cookie: DCLTYPEMENU=0
Content-type: text/html

<html><head><meta http-equiv="refresh" 
content="00;URL=main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show"></head>


As you can see, the difference is in the "Location:" header. The obvious 
reason is that Xitami can't find the file specified in the Location header 
and returns 404.
Now the question is if this is a bug or a feature. According to HTML 1.1 
definition from 
http://www.w3.org/Protocols/rfc2616/rfc2616-sec14.html#sec14.30:
"The field value consists of a single absolute URI.
       Location       = "Location" ":" absoluteURI  "
In this case the URI is definitely not an absolute one. So if this is the 
reason for the 404 error, I guess it's OK, although other users seem to be 
using this dcl software just fine. On the other hand, if for some reason 
Xitami tries, but cannot parse the "Location:" field, then it is a bug.

Thanks again,
Boyan

Each surfer can un-default IE to show "unfriendly" error messages. Of
course you can't expect strangers to do that. 

There was a report here that if your 404 error message was big, more
than 1 or 2 kilobytes, IE might show it instead of its "friendly"
message.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 17 09:05:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Tue, 17 Jul 2001 08:05:33 GMT
Subject: [Xitami] Custom Errors

In message <000901c10e88$273af180$0100a8c0@leiter1>
   "Brian Leiter" writes:

> I don't use Netscape

Whilst such an attitude might be condoned in an end-user, those designing
any web site ought to be conducting testing with at least Netscape (in
addition to IE).  If they're thorough, they ought to try some other
browsers as well, such as Opera, with a text-only browser (such as Lynx)
also used, especially for checking accessibility to the disabled (such as
those using screen-reader software).

"Designing" for IE alone is preventing half the world from having the
hope to see your site.

So even if you personally don't use Netscape whilst "surfing" yourself,
you should at least see how it (mis)behaves with your own site.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 17 17:15:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Andrew Tate)
Date: Tue, 17 Jul 2001 17:15:04 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Custom Errors
In-Reply-To: <43339@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010717171504.007ae100@pop.surrey.ac.uk>

Don't forget Xitami has an inbuilt feature to enable simple testing out for error messages - copied from the documentation it is:-

To test a specific error, you can use the special URL 'error?xxx'. For instance, to simulate a 402 error (Payment Required), use a URL like this: 

'http://127.0.0.1/error?402'. 

You can simulate a 302 error (temporary redirection) using a URL like this: 'http://127.0.0.1/error?302:/somedir/somepage.htm'.

Works for me on Win98se and with IE4 and Netscape and I get my custom error messages with header and footer complete with graphics.

Andy..

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 17 22:59:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Tue, 17 Jul 2001 16:59:15 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Perl Script
In-Reply-To: <004501c10ef5$bae794c0$0201a8c0@midco.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010717165915.007ccb10@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 02:21 PM 7/17/01 -0500, you wrote:
>I have a Perl script which performs redirection using an HTTP 'Location'
>header, and works fine on Netscape but is extremely slow to work on IE. Does
>anyone know what in Xitami could be causing this?

Are you doing site redirection
  (Location: http://wwww.someoffsiteaddress.com/somedir/index.html)
or local redirection (Location: /myonsitedir/index.html)?

If you are doing local redirection then I highly recommend using XiFusion
v2.5 as it will do both absolute (/myonsitedir/index.html) and relative
(../myonsitedir/index.html) local redirection on the server end of things.
Instead of passing the information constantly between the browser, Xitami
webserver, and your scripts, XiFusion will cut out the unnecessary
redirections (and add functionality for relative local redirections).
Granted, XiFusion is designed primarily for ColdFusion, but it will also
work with PHP (officially) and Perl (unofficially).  (XiFusion is available
for both Linux and Windows 9x/NT).

If you are performing site redirection, then it is the browser's
responsibility and XiFusion won't help your situation any.

XiFusion v2.5 can be obtained from:  <http://www.shininglightpro.com/>.
  Click Products->Intel x86->XiFusion to get to the information and
download page.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

I recently visited a website where they cunningly used the referer field 
and redirection of it was not present/not suitable to  provide a certain 
amount of security within the site without SSL or any other security 
scehme. This seemed really cool.

Is there a way to do the same thing in Xitami?
What you want to do is only display certain pages if HTTP_REFERER is set 
to an appropriate value otherwise do a redirect to the login page.

I can clearly do this in with CGI pages but I don't think I can do it 
for non CGI pages?

Any ideas

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 18 22:08:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 19 Jul 2001 09:08:05 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] referer field
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Wed, 18 Jul 2001 22:05:08 -0400." <3B564054.30802@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200107182108.JAA20264@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B564054.30802@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>I recently visited a website where they cunningly used the referer field 
>and redirection of it was not present/not suitable to  provide a certain 
>amount of security within the site without SSL or any other security 
>scehme. This seemed really cool.

It's fairly weak "security".  Anyone can set the referer field to
anything they want (or not set it) when making a request.  Also some
firewalls and web proxies remove the referer field, which could make it
impossible for some visitors to reach some parts of your website.  In
short: be careful what you apply this technique to.

>Is there a way to do the same thing in Xitami?
>What you want to do is only display certain pages if HTTP_REFERER is set 
>to an appropriate value otherwise do a redirect to the login page.

As you note, you can do this with CGIs.  You can also do it with Filters
AFAIK, as Xitami treats them basically like filters when it comes to
processing things.  And of course you can do it with LRWPs. 

But you can't do it just with plain HTML files at present.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

ites:
>I just got a cable modem and now Xitami can't see the ip address.

configuration menus.  It's usually called a "pinhole" or "port forwarding".

In message <FNEAKJNHKIFEIAHOLMPCMEJMCCAA.Joe@ByrneWorld.com>, "ByrneWorld" writes:
>I just upgraded one of my servers (WinNT 4-sp6) with the latest service
>version, 2.5b1.  

2.5b1 is NOT the latest service version; it's an old beta version.
2.4d9 is the latest release version of Xitami.  2.5b5 is the latest beta
version.

"2.5b1" has some known bugs so you might want to at least try 2.5b5
(which also has some known bugs, but fewer/different from 2.5b5).

>Doing some investigating, the POST parameters are not being passed.  I 
>looked through the xitami.cfg file but I'm not sure there is anything 
>there that I want to change without some help.

As a start try turning on CGI debugging ([CGI] debug=1), and have a look
at the .cgi and .cgo files.

Ewen

PS: We'd appreciate it if you didn't send winmail.dat attachments to
    this mailing list; plain text is the preferred format.

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>file.  The control panel is just blank where it says hits but other data is
>okay.

Ah.  That one is more of a problem, because the control panel in NT runs
in a separate memory space from the webserver (unlike the GUI console
version where it's all part of the same program).

So the answer to "will it work" is "not easily", alas.  

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul 22 10:58:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jerry Richer)
Date: Sun, 22 Jul 2001 05:58:50 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Cable modem
References: <20010721050227.47940.qmail@web10905.mail.yahoo.com> <3B590F5F.AF6EA36@evernet.net>
Message-ID: <00e601c11296$3b2724e0$6401a8c0@bur.adelphia.net>

     I use a device like the Linksys router.  Mine is the CNIG904B from
CNET.  It is connected to my cable modem then their are four computers
plugged into the CNIG904B.  There's no Internet sharing software required.
The router takes care of everything.  For setup just plug a computer into
the CNIG904B and with your browser go to: http://192.168.1.1,  Fill out the
form you'll get for that particular machine.  One of the questions on the
form is asking if you want this particular computer to get it's IP address
automatically or do you want it to be assigned?  I have three of my
computers set to get it automatically and one set to it it assigned.  The
one that has it assigned is my Xitami server machine and I believe for a
server an assigned IP address is required.  The IP address I assigned it has
to be one of 192.168.1.1 through 192.168.1.4, I believe.  When traffic flows
between any of the four computers and the cable modem the router knows what
machine it came from and is going to.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 23 04:26:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sun, 22 Jul 2001 22:26:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] how add a mail server to xitami
In-Reply-To: <15ONQ2-0AiM9wC@fmrl05.sul.t-online.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010722222621.007d1820@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 07:52 PM 7/22/01 +0200, you wrote:
>Hello,
>
>there are some cgi as well as php files which deal with handling of
>forms via e-mail send back to a specified e-mail address ... is there a
>simple way of adding a mail server or something to Xitami so I can test
>those functions locally as well ...? 
>
>(I did get the CGI stuff working ... so it seems; but I could not find
>any info in the Xitami help about mailserver or mails etc. )
>God bless you with His grace and peace 
>Wolfgang 

Try the "1st Class Mailserver" (http://www.1cis.com).  It sticks a fairly
non-intrusive footer onto all outgoing messages and is extremely easy to
set up.  However, I've never been able to figure out how to bring it down
without rebooting.  It consumes a very small amount of memory, and is
fairly fast.  There are other mailservers out there, but they take a while
to set up and not all are free.  Beware, the shareware version of 1cis is
SPAM-prone and offers no protection from outsiders.  If you want a more
permanent solution, then I recommend trying EzMTS (www.ezmts.org - the
freeware version).  You still need some CGI-based solution to actually talk
to the mail server, but at least you would have a test server to work with.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 23 18:24:10 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 23 Jul 2001 13:24:10 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] how add a mail server to xitami
References: <15Og5H-1iQTa4C@fmrl06.sul.t-online.com>
Message-ID: <3B5C5DBA.FB44ED0F@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Or does this "mailserver" really have nothing to do with the "xitami webserver" ?  

Nothing at all to do with the webserver, except the sendmail program
probably should run on the same machine as your scripts. 

Machines can have MANY "servers". HTTP, FTP, mail, time, telnet, DNS,
.....  Xitami combines HTTP and FTP, which is unusual (FTP is far older
than HTTP); for it to add email service would be nice but a bit much. 

The internet, email, and unix grew up together in the same time and
places. So unix machines almost always have a suite of mail services.

Windows grew up un-networked, or with MicroSoft's strange windows-only
mail system, or with clients that did as little as possible to get/send
mail through a real mail server. Also, Windows isn't about command-line
work. So Windows lacks mail tools that most unix boxes have.

The core mail program is a post office, a program to accept, sort,
store, and deliver mail. This generally runs in the background and you
do not talk to it directly. 

To send mail, unix has sendmail, a very simple program to accept a
formatted file and submit it to a post office. The docs for sendmail say
that it isn't made for use by people, a front-end program is needed to
get a nice user interface. But on a script that knows what sendmail
needs, it is the standard way to send mail.

Users on unix systems use mail (a very simple command-line program),
Pine/Elm/etc which are text-mode menu-driven full-screen email managers,
and fancier stuff. Good for people, and you could drive mail with a
script, but overkill for most script work.

There are BIG security risks in running mail services. The biggest is
the post office: traditionally such programs accept mail from strangers
and deliver it anywhere. Spammers love these, because "you" get the
blame for their spam. I would be real wary of some post office from
unknown authors, with mystery options and unknown bugs. Also, older
emailers may not block newly discovered hacker tricks. Craig's program
looks excellent, but read the docs well and be sure to talk to him or
experienced postmasters to be sure your postoffice is secure.

If you just want script-driven mail sending, you may not need your own
post office. Your ISP surely runs a postofffice and should accept email
from machines on internal IP numbers (or with authentication). Configure
sendmail to submit mail through your ISP's post office. I found one for
Windows that can do this, but it is exceptionally hard to set up, and
the usual perl script must be hacked to feed it right. I'll probably
move to a full mail suite the next time this one frustrates me. 

(I'm shocked that there does not seem to be a "universal" sendmail
written directly in Perl. The net::SMTP module has the essentials, and I
have a rough draft working under Windows, but with hard-coded message
headers and body, not in the way sendmail expects.)

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 23 20:58:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 23 Jul 2001 15:58:15 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] how add a mail server to xitami
References: <15OkC4-0tuyciC@fmrl02.sul.t-online.com>
Message-ID: <3B5C81D7.2EC525D6@rci.rutgers.edu>

>   a program I can run on my win2k machine without being connected to the internet and for testing of certain e-mail functions in my websites which I am testing ...  

OH!

You don't need email? You need something to catch what a script sends to
sendmail? 

Create a plain text file, named SENDMAIL.BAT , and put this line in it:

 more >> C:\sentmail.txt

Save SENDMAIL.BAT "someplace". Where? Since most perl scripts using
sendmail assume it is some place like /usr/bin , you could try making a
folder of that name on the same drive as Xitami, and put it there. OR,
put it some place you like and edit your perl scripts to point to it.
Whichever is easier. 

For initial testing, find or make a small text file and copy it to the
same folder as SENDMAIL.BAT. Let's say the text file is called TEST.TXT. 
Open a DOS window and CD to that folder. The command 

  SENDMAIL < TEST.TXT

should run without complaint. Now look for the file C:\sentmail.txt and
open it. Should contain the words in TEST.TXT. Each time you run
SENDMAIL, the text sent through it will be appended to the end of
C:\SENTMAIL.TXT

Then try your scripts. 

I *think* that will emulate enough of a real sendmail to do what you
want.

 -PRR

WHATEVER | MORE.

Owen Rudge

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 24 00:21:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 24 Jul 2001 11:21:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Moving Cgi-bin dir
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jordan Bassett" <flare_storm@yahoo.com>
 of "Sun, 22 Jul 2001 23:27:09 MST." <JBEBLMMBAAIAEILFEPDIEEAGCBAA.flare_storm@yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200107232321.LAA32644@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <JBEBLMMBAAIAEILFEPDIEEAGCBAA.flare_storm@yahoo.com>, "Jordan Bassett" writes:
>I want to move my cgi-bin directory to a completely different part of my
>hard drive.  I have tried changing the cgi option in the console and
>defaults.cfg to c:\dir with spaces\folder\cgi-bin.  But the testcgi program
>gives a page with "Cannot create cgi process - program not found" .  

Chances are this is because of "\dir with spaces\", and the (poor) way
that Microsoft handles this situation.  We do try to work around this
problem, but it's not 100%.  I'd suggest trying an alternative
directory path _without_ spaces in its name.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 24 05:37:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 24 Jul 2001 00:37:37 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] how add a mail server to xitami
References: <15OkC4-0tuyciC@fmrl02.sul.t-online.com> <3B5C81D7.2EC525D6@rci.rutgers.edu> <3B5CDC98.9020409@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <3B5CFB91.F4A0CE29@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Umm - if  you are creating more than 25 line mail messages I think you'll have a stalled program waiting for someone to press
enter 

Duh - I hadn't thought of that. I just was not thinking of MORE's
main feature (the 25-line pause) at all.

But it seems Owen is right. I just ran 240+ lines through my BAT
file in a single gulp, and all the output showed as soon as I
switched back to my editor (which told me I should reload the
changed file). 

Theory: MORE asks the terminal driver how many lines between
Press Any Key.... 25, 43, 50 lines, it can vary. When run in a
pipe, the answer is "There is no screen size", and apparently
MORE is smart enough (or stupid enough) to pass huge streams
without user intervention.

 ....More testing... I just fed it 34480 lines, 1.1 megabytes.
This takes a couple seconds, and then the output shows up in the
sentmail.txt file. 30K lines+ and a megabyte+ of characters ought
to be enough for most purposes. 

I learned something new. Thanks. 

Owen > if you do TYPE WHATEVER | MORE

I tried TYPE, but sendmail generally expects the body of the
message as a pipe or redirect. I could not remember the syntax to
make TYPE eat STDIN instead of a real file. (DOS ain't unix; and
TYPE predates the semi-unixification of DOS 2.0.) 

Wolfgang, if you are still here... sendmail also generally takes
the TO address and some arcane options on the command line. My
trick will not pass this information. I assume that, since you
aren't really mailing it, you don't need this info while doing
"sandbox by myself" testing. You will check your TO address and
options in the script when you really do set it up for emailing.

Also: the "fake" sendmail dumping to a local text file is faster
than any mail server. True, a local unloaded mailserver can be
faster than your fingers so that may not be important, but the
fake sendmail is probably many microseconds faster. And keeping a
good editor open on the output file is probably faster than
working through a mail reader. Especially on a pay-per-minute
connection.

>OH! > Oooh, Paul!

Sorry. I didn't mean to startle you. But I was so excited I
slapped my forehead and said "OH! That's what he needs!"

I was not sure what you were doing, and you were not sure what to
ask, so we had all that talk about mailservers. When it became
clear that you were "testing in a sandbox", and wanted to work
off-line, and real email wasn't needed, I said "OH! There has to
be some super-simple way to do that!" 

You didn't need a mail server, you needed something to pretend to
take mail (in sendmail format) and put it where you could see it.
As long as the script can believe it is feeding to sendmail, it
does not matter what really happens inside "sendmail". DOS isn't
unix so it isn't THAT easy, but certainly a BAT file with MORE is
easier than building a post office. 

If you ever do install a "real" sendmail, hide or rename your
"fake" sendmail so there is no confusion. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 24 22:10:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 09:10:26 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Php
In-Reply-To: Message from "Richard Donahue" <rdonahue10@home.com>
 of "Tue, 24 Jul 2001 16:04:24 EST." <00aa01c11484$386eab20$0201a8c0@midco.net>
Message-ID: <200107242110.JAA12823@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <00aa01c11484$386eab20$0201a8c0@midco.net>, "Richard Donahue" writes:
>PHP 4.0.6, Xitami 2.4c3 Pro and Windows NT 4 workstation.
>In filters I have:
>.php=c:/php
>
>In the php.ini I edited:
>doc_root = c:\xitami\webpages
>extension_dir = c:\php
>
>When trying to access a test php all I get is "The page cannot be displayed"

Check cgierr.log.

I strongly suspect you don't actually have a c:\php _program_ for Xitami
to run (which is what you're telling it to run) and that's the problem.

You need to point the filter at the _program_ doing the filtering, not
just a directory that might happen to contain it somewhere.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 25 02:39:42 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (garry)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 13:39:42 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Php
References: <00a001c11480$8e8d9f60$0201a8c0@midco.net>
Message-ID: <001e01c114aa$ad41c8d0$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>

hi i recently had to install php for one of my users, and knowing nothing
about it, went to the php site and found an installer file for php4

reading the info it said it worked for win with iis pws and xitami

of course i downloaded it and ran it but there was nothing in xitami

this turned out to be because i had a version that was running in the xiwin
dir and the new versions all run in the xitami dir

i downloaded the upgrade installed restarted and reinstalled php and it just
worked.

the file i downloaded was called php-4.0.3pl1-installer.exe

try it, you will all like it. and it will save you so much time posting
here.

for those not using xitami running from the xitami dir be aware that in
doing my upgrade i lost ssi and had to upgrade to the latest version to get
it back.


Garry Stanley

Cable.net.nz

Beta Data Solutions Ltd.
