From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 25 05:24:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Tue, 24 Jul 2001 23:24:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Php
In-Reply-To: <3B5E2360.D8D892E0@evernet.net>
References: <200107242110.JAA12823@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
 <5.1.0.14.2.20010724174335.009e34d0@192.168.0.4>
 <00be01c11490$675d52e0$0201a8c0@midco.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010724232453.0079cae0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 06:39 PM 7/24/01 -0700, you wrote:
>http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm
>
>Try the XiFusion plug in...never used it with PHP but it's supposed
>to help make that work too...just an idea..

XiFusion will work with that version of Xitami, but requires another
wrapper for it to work correctly.  I'm experimenting with that particular
version of Pro as well, so here is a Perl wrapper for you to use (Requires
Perl, PHP, and XiFusion):

#!c:/perl/bin/perl

$ENV{"PATH_TRANSLATED"} = $ENV{"DOCUMENT_ROOT"}.$ENV{"SCRIPT_NAME"};
# You might need to modify the following line:
system "c:\\xifusion\\xifusion.exe c:\\php4\\php.exe";


In the Filters section, use something like this:
  .php=c:\perl\bin\perl c:\progra~1\xitamipro\nvmlwrap.pl

I know it isn't pretty, but it works.

Hope that helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

>page.

Dear Rich,

I have a win2k (formerly a Win98) system with Xitami and PHP running
very well and without trouble.

(1) Installed PHP for Win (download install file from www.php.net) in
      the "normal" directory c:\php

(2) In Xitami, I then edited the {Filters] section in the *.cfg files
for 
      the virutal hosts and defaults.cfg as follows:

     [Filter]
    .php=c:\php\php.exe
    .php3=c:\php\php.exe
    .phtml=c:\php\php.exe 

After that, I could call up any domain (virtual host) and use php files
with the above file extensions and they run without any trouble or
error messages.
(of course, the domains / virtual hosts need to be entered in the Win
HOSTS file to be recognized with "localhost"

God bless you with His grace and peace 
Wolfgang

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 25 13:23:47 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 13:23:47 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Php
References: <200107242110.JAA12823@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz> <00b401c11488$95d29c00$0201a8c0@midco.net>
Message-ID: <005d01c11504$a94972a0$de98fc3e@rudge>

> and in my browser (IE5) I get a blank page with :

I've had that problem on a couple of systems and it's very annoying!
However, I got it to work by:

1) Installing PHP to C:\PHP (it shouldn't matter where it is installed)
2) Copying PHP.EXE and PHP4TS.DLL to the Xitami directory
3) Adding:

.php=php.exe
.php3=php.exe

to the [Filter] section of the appropriate CFG file.

Owen Rudge
http://www.owenrudge.co.uk/
http://www.gamearchive.uk.tt/

People, you have to pay attention to the version of Xitami this guy is
using.  It has NOTHING to do with PHP!  Instead, it is how the CGI/Filter
environment is set up before running PHP.  The version he is using creates
a slightly different environment compared to the latest builds of Xitami
thus causing PHP to not work.

>  here is a Perl wrapper for you to use

On DOS-based machines, a BAT file can do the same and probably with less
overhead. Launching an instance of Perl needs a couple megs of RAM; an
instance of COMMAND (or CMD) to process a BAT file is under 64K. 

I doubt there is a practical difference unless you run a P-133 with
32Megs, as I was doing until this week. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 25 23:45:35 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 26 Jul 2001 10:45:35 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] problem n apology
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jeff Scarlets" <jeff@scar.ath.cx>
 of "Wed, 25 Jul 2001 08:57:06 MST." <001601c11522$74977980$69209cca@PROZAK>
Message-ID: <200107252245.KAA29083@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001601c11522$74977980$69209cca@PROZAK>, "Jeff Scarlets" writes:
>it just came to my attention that my mailing list server is causing 
>problems. on my local mail server i set the alias to send mail to 
>jeff@scarlets.ath.cx to my actual account. however i did not realize 
>that there is a loop within. i have removed the server and hopefully 
>fixed the problem.

Thanks.  You came very close to being removed from the list, and
possibly banned from it: mail configuration errors that send their error
messages back to the list are very bad, and ones that then process their
own input (ie, feeding on their own problems) are very very bad.

(For those wondering I was doing little things like sleeping, which is
why it didn't get removed earlier.  Sorry for the inconvenience.)

Anyway planning on forwarding messages from the mailing list somewhere
should be _very_ careful to test it properly, and monitor it in case
something goes wrong.  And very very careful that it doesn't send error
messages back to the mailing list, or people who post to thel list.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> own input (ie, feeding on their own problems) are very very bad.
>
> (For those wondering I was doing little things like sleeping, which is
> why it didn't get removed earlier.  Sorry for the inconvenience.)
>
> Anyway planning on forwarding messages from the mailing list somewhere
> should be _very_ careful to test it properly, and monitor it in case
> something goes wrong.  And very very careful that it doesn't send error
> messages back to the mailing list, or people who post to thel list.
>
> Ewen
>

> Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 27 04:08:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 26 Jul 2001 22:08:46 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4 Problems..
In-Reply-To: <3B60ABC9.C51A4A86@esite-me.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010726220846.007d1c20@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 04:46 PM 7/26/01 -0700, you wrote:
>index.php file is <?  header("Location: menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0");
>?>.  In checking the debug files, it does seem to find and read the

If you want to use relative 'Location:' headers like you have above, you
will need to use XiFusion as Xitami (latest stable release) does not
support server-side redirection, thus the 'Location:' must either be
absolute (header("Location: /fw/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0");) OR you use
XiFusion as it will handle the server-side redirections (both relative and
absolute) correctly.

>file, but it's output size is 0.  I tried to parse it via the command

XiFusion will always guarantee at least 1 byte of HTML output...that way
IE/Netscape/etc. does not "hang" waiting for a page to return.

>line, but got nothing.  I also tried
>http://localhost/fw/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0, but it did not work.

That's odd.  What exactly happened when you ran that script (logfile data,
debug info., etc.)?

                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 27 22:49:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 27 Jul 2001 17:49:48 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Re: SSI Implementation: buggy?
References: <200107271425590.SM00258@default>
Message-ID: <3B61E1FC.C5AF2E29@rci.rutgers.edu>

> "Is Xitami's SSI implimentation buggy or incomplete?", 

Are we talking 2.4 or 2.5?

2.4's SSI is stated to be incomplete, but is just a Perl script which
you could edit to add any feature you need. 

> I have reviewed several SSI tutorials from the net... the set command is not described very often,

I'm no SSI expert, but is it possible that SSI set is something invented
by Apache? Considering Apache's dominance in the webserver world,
tutorials may not bother to mention if something works only on Apache. 

For what it's worth: "set" is NOT documented on the NCSA site's SSI
page, the birthplace of CGI and SSI. 

http://hoohoo.ncsa.uiuc.edu/docs/tutorials/includes.html

The NCSA site is referenced in Xitami 2.4's docs at /xitami/INDEX6.HTM,
which does not list "set" but adds: "With a small knowledge of Perl, you
can easily modify the Perlssi filter to add support for other tags." 

Obviously if you don't want to hack some Perl, and nobody here has a
pre-tested PerlSSI "set" modification you can use, that's no use. 

Xitami 2.5 has in-built SSI, which I have not looked at. If "set" really
is a commonly used extension of SSI, maybe Ewen should know. 

> I recognize that Apache also is not the be-all and end-all of 
webserver software

Well, but it IS the dominant server by a good margin. Each of us has our
own reasons for picking a server; I'd say that a need for 99.99% Apache
compatibility is a good reason to use Apache. They have ports to most
platforms. All free. 

They say the Windows port may be unstable, but it appears to be as
stable as anything on Windows can be. I think they disclaim it just so
they don't tarnish the reliability reputation Apache has running on
clean unix boxes. Certainly WinApache should be stable enough for hard
development duty. And it isn't significantly bigger than Xitami; the
main drawback is arcane configuration files to edit. But I had the
basics working pretty easy. 

  -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 27 23:33:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 28 Jul 2001 10:33:56 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Re: SSI Implementation: buggy?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Julian Rickards" <jrickards@tyenet.com>
 of "Fri, 27 Jul 2001 14:08:47 -0400." <200107271425590.SM00258@default>
Message-ID: <200107272233.KAA10592@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <200107271425590.SM00258@default>, "Julian Rickards" writes:
>Although no one has yet answered my question, "Is Xitami's SSI 
>implimentation buggy or incomplete?", I have determined that, for 
>whatever reason, Xitami won't or can't impliment SSI's #set command 
>but the same code works under Apache 1.3.20.

AFAIK the #set command is an Apache extension; if you require that
Apache extension then I guess you'll have to use Apache :-)

There has been some discussion about extending the Xitami SSI handler
(which is based on the NCSA include facility; Apache was originally
based on the NCSA code too), in particular extending it to support some
of the common Apache and other extensions, but this has not happened.

As always we welcome someone taking the time to write the code to handle
the extensions.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 27 23:37:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 28 Jul 2001 10:37:06 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] SSI Implementation: buggy?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Julian Rickards" <jrickards@tyenet.com>
 of "Thu, 26 Jul 2001 16:27:24 -0400." <200107261643255.SM00258@default>
Message-ID: <200107272237.KAA10745@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <200107261643255.SM00258@default>, "Julian Rickards" writes:
>I have reviewed several SSI tutorials from the net but although the 
>set command is not described very often, from the few that I found 
>that described its use, it would appear that I am using it correctly.  I 
>am wondering if Xitami's implementation of SSI is either deficient or 
>has a bug in it.

Xitami's SSI is not Apache's extended SSI.  If you call that
"incomplete" then I guess it's "incomplete".  But it never claimed to be
an implementation of the Apache extended SSI.

>However, I want the QUERY_STRING text, in this case a filename, to 
>be the virtual filename as follows:
>
><!--#include virtual="QUERY_STRING" -->

That is becuase you ask for a file called "QUERY_STRING" to be included;
probably you don't have one.

>When my instructor for my webmaster course showed us this trick, 
>he used a slightly different procedure whereby he "set" the contents 
>of a variable to be the QUERY_STRING as follows:
>
><!--#set var="bodycontentfile" value="$QUERY_STRING" -->

As far as I know variable interpolation is also an extension to the
SSI processing, and as such it's not supported by Xitami.

As I said in another message, if you need extensions that are
implemented only in one webserver, then, well, you'll need to use that
webserver.

Offers to implement these extensions for Xitami are always welcome.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 28 21:16:30 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sat, 28 Jul 2001 15:16:30 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] reply from localhost *sometimes* slow?
In-Reply-To: <3B604164.50211026@dtbakerprojects.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010728151630.007b4500@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 10:12 AM 7/26/01 -0600, you wrote:
>something I've been wondering for a while.... Sometimes when I request a
>page that is on my //localhost, the browser takes several (2-10) seconds
>to get a reply, but other times it is really speedy.
>
>Is there something in my configuration of xitami or networking control
>panel that I can check to help my machine find localhost quickly all the
>time? My internet connection is thru @home which has no gateway defined,
>no DNS (they use DCHP enabled), dynamic IP addresses and the like.
>additionally, I just added a dlink 713p wireless router/firewall so I
>can share my connection between two home computers and have home file
>sharing.

Are you typing '//localhost' into the browser?  If so, then you should note
that it might be looking for a machine called 'localhost' using the NetBIOS
protocol (hence the really long delays).  Try the fully qualified
'http://localhost/' URL instead.  Also try 'http://127.0.0.1/' as well.

Also, I don't see how you get out onto other servers if you don't have a
gateway defined.  I'll bet a gateway shows up if you run 'winipcfg' and
select your network card.  I would even bet you have DNS as well.  DHCP is
just a protocol to set up gateway, IP address, DNS server list, WINS, etc.
information.  DHCP just makes all of that transparent to you, but it can
come in quite handy at times to know that information.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 28 22:01:58 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Sat, 28 Jul 2001 16:01:58 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] reply from localhost *sometimes* slow?
References: <3B604164.50211026@dtbakerprojects.com>
Message-ID: <3B632846.B9E8B023@2cah.com>

Look for a file called HOSTS on your system, under Win98 it should be located
in your C:\Windows\system32 directory (I think, its been a while for me under
Win9x). There is a sample file called HOSTS.SAM that is an example file for
HOSTS if you don't have it there already. 

At any rate, add the following line to your HOSTS file:

127.0.0.1	localhost

HOSTS is always checked first by Windows when it is trying to resolve
hostnames. That should help you.

Dan Baker wrote:
> 
> something I've been wondering for a while.... Sometimes when I request a
> page that is on my //localhost, the browser takes several (2-10) seconds
> to get a reply, but other times it is really speedy.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 30 10:30:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 30 Jul 2001 04:30:59 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] php-files not found on server....
In-Reply-To: <NEBBJEPFPIGHFPCNGBGCAEMBCBAA.tromp@tromp.cx>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010730043059.007c79e0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 03:54 AM 7/30/01 +0200, you wrote:
>I installed version 2.4d9 and files that are on my server are reported 
>missing......

Not sure what the problem here is - perhaps you could explain in more
detail as to what steps you have taken so far.

>I did try to install XiFusion, but i can't get it right because the readme
in 
>this .zip i downloaded, tells me about an installationprocess
non-existing. Also 
>some files that should be in the xifusion\bin aren't there.....

I think you mean ColdFusion ('cfusion\bin') when you say 'xifusion\bin'.
Remember that XiFusion is designed primarily for ColdFusion, but will also
work with PHP.  ColdFusion installs in the 'c:\cfusion' directory by
default.  XiFusion doesn't care where it is as it is a self-contained
executable (you could put it in c:\program files\myfavoritegames and it
won't care as long as it is someplace on your hard drive).

I interleaved PHP notes in with the ColdFusion installation information
since PHP is officially supported, but it isn't the primary/original use of
XiFusion.  You just need to pay some attention to the ColdFusion notes as
they will help to set up PHP, but don't follow every word since the PHP
notes are there to help set up PHP correctly.

Provide more details as to what you have so far (Filters section and the
location of XiFusion as well as the location of PHP) and I'll see what went
wrong and fix it.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 31 07:25:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Tue, 31 Jul 2001 01:25:04 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] php-files not found on server....
In-Reply-To: <NEBBJEPFPIGHFPCNGBGCMEMCCBAA.tromp@tromp.cx>
References: <3.0.6.32.20010730043059.007c79e0@pop.crosswinds.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010731012504.007d0660@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 12:46 PM 7/30/01 +0200, you wrote:
>I am running xitami version 2.4d9 on windows98 with mysql and php. After
>installing xitami, the perlinstaller and mysql i get  the message that some
>php-files could not be located on my server. I am however very sure the are
>where they should be. In the xitami archieves i found some messages that it
>could be that passing unfilled variables could cause this and that xifusion
>solved the problem. So i downloaded xifusion.zip.
>
>In the readme file in this zip, is said that during the installationprocess
>a xifusion\bin dir is created with a program, later needed in the
>installationprocess of xifusion.

You are referring to the lines that say:
PHP NOTE:  The line in the [Filter] section should look like this:
           .php=c:\cfusion\bin\XiFusion c:\php\php.exe

I assumed that XiFusion was installed in the c:\cfusion\bin directory when
I wrote the documentation.  You have to *manually* extract XiFusion.exe and
put it into a directory somewhere on your hard drive and replace
'c:\cfusion\bin' with the drive and directory where you put the XiFusion
executable (XiFusion.exe).  Note that there is NO fancy install program as
there is really only one necessary file and a 1MB installation program is
hardly necessary for a 65K executable.

BTW, this format of documentation is quite standard for DOS/Console
programs.  DOS is simple to use, but you have to know to translate path
names/drive letters in your head when reading readme.txt files since no two
computer systems are set up exactly the same.  XiFusion is really a Win32
Console mode program, thus I wrote the documentation using DOS
documentation standards in mind.

Also, when you start to work with web servers and interfacing CGI
applications (which is what PHP and ColdFusion really are), knowledge of
how to use DOS comes in quite handy.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

Date: Wed, 25 Apr 2001 20:14:49 -0500
From: Ewen McNeill <ewen@imatix.com >
Reply-To: Xitami@EC-Computers.Net
To: Xitami@ec-computers.net
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4.04 and Alias

In message <3AE75787.2581B4BD@infotech.monash.edu.au>, Lee Seldon writes:
>I can't seem to get PHP4 scripts to work in an Alias directory.

Aliases, and filters (if that's how you're using PHP; CGIs for that
matter) do not mix together very well. You're better off using some
other approach (eg, virtual hosts) to handle the virtual directories if
you need to use PHP/CGI with them.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 31 10:53:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 31 Jul 2001 21:53:59 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Files deleted ??? Intrusion ?
In-Reply-To: Message from DanLM <Dan_LM@yahoo.com>
 of "Tue, 31 Jul 2001 11:47:37 +0200." <5.0.2.1.0.20010731113544.00a6e600@mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200107310953.VAA00870@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <5.0.2.1.0.20010731113544.00a6e600@mail.yahoo.com>, DanLM writes:
>I have this strange information in my "xitami.log" file:
>2001/07/30 09:08:49: 2 files deleted in directory './logs'
>2001/07/30 10:08:50: 2 files deleted in directory './logs'
>2001/07/30 11:08:50: 2 files deleted in directory './logs'
>2001/07/30 12:08:50: 2 files deleted in directory './logs'

This is normal, although it seems that your files are being rotated
fairly often.  Basically this message is from xisuper, the "supervisor"
of Xitami, and it is expiring old log files which are older than the
expiry time that you've sent.

Curiously it seems to be expiring two of them per hour, which suggests
that your log files (or at least one of two of them) are being rolled
over hourly.  That seems a little often to be rolling over the log files
to me; I tend to use weekly, or daily on busy sites.

But no, it's not someone breaking in.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
